        </div><div class="casAbstract">It is widely accepted that for elec. vehicles to be accepted by consumers and to achieve wide market penetration, ranges of at least 500 km at an affordable cost are required.  Therefore, significant improvements to lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) in terms of energy d. and cost along the battery value chain are required, while other key performance indicators, such as lifetime, safety, fast-charging ability and low-temp. performance, need to be enhanced or at least sustained.  Here, we review advances and challenges in LIB materials for automotive applications, in particular with respect to cost and performance parameters.  The prodn. processes of anode and cathode materials are discussed, focusing on material abundance and cost.  Advantages and challenges of different types of electrolyte for automotive batteries are examd.  Finally, energy densities and costs of promising battery chemistries are critically evaluated along with an assessment of the potential to fulfil the ambitious targets of elec. vehicle propulsion.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrXUrHzsP37n7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgsGT5oo0-_Aw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXos1KhtLs%253D&amp;md5=4b9155ce46053d996fa7e45636dea8f0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref2'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit2" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2014.03.155"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ahmad, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Facile Synthesis of Single-Crystal Mesoporous CoNiO<sub>2</sub> Nanosheets Assembled Flowers as Anode Materials for Lithium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Electrochim. Acta</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>132</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">404</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">409</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.electacta.2014.03.155</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D132%26publication_year%3D2014%26pages%3D404-409%26journal%3DElectrochim.%2BActa%26author%3DY.%2BLiu%26author%3DY.%2BZhao%26author%3DY.%2BYu%26author%3DM.%2BAhmad%26author%3DH.%2BSun%26title%3DFacile%2BSynthesis%2Bof%2BSingle-Crystal%2BMesoporous%2BCoNiO2%2BNanosheets%2BAssembled%2BFlowers%2Bas%2BAnode%2BMaterials%2Bfor%2BLithium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.electacta.2014.03.155&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c18269&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.electacta.2014.03.155&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Facile synthesis of single-crystal mesoporous CoNiO2 nanosheets assembled flowers as anode materials for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yanguo; Zhao, Yanyan; Yu, Yanlong; Ahmad, Mashkoor; Sun, Hongyu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">132</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">404-409</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Mesoporous CoNiO2 microflowers assembled with single-crystal nanosheets were successfully synthesized by a hydrothermal method and subsequent annealing process and their Li storage capacity were studied.  The structural and compositional anal. of the mesoporous CoNiO2 microflowers was studied by x-ray diffraction, field emission SEM and high-resoln. TEM.  The Bruauer-Emmett-Teller sp. surface area of CoNiO2 microflowers was calcd. by the N isotherm curve and pore size distribution was detd. by the Barret-Joyner-Halenda method.  The as-prepd. CoNiO2 electrodes delivered satisfied capacity, good cycling stability and rate capability.  The improved electrochem. performance is attributed to the mesoporous nature and the 3-dimensional assembled structure.  Therefore, such a structure can be considered to be an attractive candidate as an electrode material for Li-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqt0wOlWGeMYLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgsGT5oo0-_Aw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXos1ensrg%253D&amp;md5=cdb88ce816f50a7d0884e1fedc8c8bae</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref3'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit3" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201702779"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mukhopadhyay, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hafez, A.                         cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Effects of alloying element Ca on the corrosion behavior and bioactivity of anodic films formed on AM60 Mg alloys</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Anawati, Anawati; Asoh, Hidetaka; Ono, Sachiko</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Effects of alloying element Ca on the corrosion behavior and bioactivity of films formed by plasma electrolytic oxidn. (PEO) on AM60 alloys were investigated.  The corrosion behavior was studied by conducting electrochem. tests in 0.9% NaCl soln. while the bioactivity was evaluated by soaking the specimens in simulated body fluid (SBF).  Under identical anodization conditions, the PEO film thicknesses increased with increasing Ca content in the alloys, which enhanced the corrosion resistance in NaCl soln.  Thicker apatite layers grew on the PEO films of Ca-contg. alloys because Ca was incorporated into the PEO film and because Ca was present in the alloys.  Improvement of corrosion resistance and bioactivity of the PEO-coated AM60 by alloying with Ca may be beneficial for biodegradable implant applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGourF4RgHVqeLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgsGT5oo0-_Aw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXht1Kktr3F&amp;md5=b4f71eb20c94cf1e194d7252fe4e36ac</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref5'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit5" data-doi="10.1021/acs.accounts.5b00482"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bommier, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Na-Ion Battery Anodes: Materials and Electrochemistry</span>. <i>Acc.                         cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na-Ion Battery Anodes: Materials and Electrochemistry</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Luo, Wei; Shen, Fei; Bommier, Clement; Zhu, Hongli; Ji, Xiulei; Hu, Liangbing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Accounts of Chemical Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">49</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">231-240</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ACHRE4</span>;

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The intermittent nature of renewable energy sources, such as solar and wind, calls for sustainable elec. energy storage (EES) technologies for stationary applications.  Li will be simply too rare for Li-ion batteries (LIBs) to be used for large-scale storage purposes.  In contrast, Na-ion batteries (NIBs) are highly promising to meet the demand of grid-level storage because Na is truly earth abundant and ubiquitous around the globe.  Furthermore, NIBs share a similar rocking-chair operation mechanism with LIBs, which potentially provides high reversibility and long cycling life.  It would be most efficient to transfer knowledge learned on LIBs during the last three decades to the development of NIBs.  Following this logic, rapid progress has been made in NIB cathode materials, where layered metal oxides and polyanionic compds. exhibit encouraging results.  On the anode side, pure graphite as the std. anode for LIBs can only form NaC64 in NIBs if solvent co-intercalation does not occur due to the unfavorable thermodn.  In fact, it was the utilization of a carbon anode in LIBs that enabled the com. successes.  Anodes of metal-ion batteries det. key characteristics, such as safety and cycling life; thus, it is indispensable to identify suitable anode materials for NIBs.In this Account, we review recent development on anode materials for NIBs.  Due to the limited space, we will mainly discuss carbon-based and alloy-based anodes and highlight progress made in our groups in this field.  We first present what is known about the failure mechanism of graphite anode in NIBs.  We then go on to discuss studies on hard carbon anodes, alloy-type anodes, and org. anodes.  Esp., the multiple functions of natural cellulose that is used as a low-cost carbon precursor for mass prodn. and as a soft substrate for tin anodes are highlighted.  The strategies of minimizing the surface area of carbon anodes for improving the first-cycle Coulombic efficiency are also outlined, where graphene oxide was employed as dehydration agent and 2,2,6,6-tetramethylpiperidine-1-oxyl (TEMPO) was used to unzip wood fiber.  Furthermore, surface modification by at. layer deposition technol. is introduced, where we discover that a thin layer of Al2O3 can function to encapsulate Sn nanoparticles, leading to a much enhanced cycling performance.  We also highlight recent work about the phosphorene/graphene anode, which outperformed other anodes in terms of capacity.  The arom. org. anode is also studied as anode with very high initial sodiation capacity.  Furthermore, electrochem. intercalation of Na ions into reduced graphene oxide is applied for fabricating transparent conductors, demonstrating the great feasibility of Na ion intercalation for optical applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGorKnQvVSK3P7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgdF_8CpJO00g"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A sandwich structure of mesoporous anatase TiO2 sheets and reduced graphene oxide and its application as lithium-ion battery electrodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Bai, Lu; Fang, Fang; Zhao, Yanyan; Liu, Yanguo; Li, Jinpeng; Huang, Guoyong; Sun, Hongyu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">RSC Advances</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Mesoporous anatase TiO2 sheets/rGO sandwich-like nanocomposites were facile synthesized by acid-assisted tetra-Bu titanate hydrolysis and subsequent thermal redn. process. When used as the anode materials of Li-ion batteries, the as-prepd. sample delivered reasonable capacity, good cycling stability and rate capability.  The optimal sample delivered a high reversible lithium-storage capacity of ∼161.4 mA h g-1 after 50 cycles at a current rate of 0.5 C (1 C = 335 mA g-1), with good cycling stability and rate capability.                         cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hard Carbons for Sodium-Ion Battery Anodes: Synthetic Strategies, Material Properties, and Storage Mechanisms</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wahid, Malik; Puthusseri, Dhanya; Gawli, Yogesh; Sharma, Neha; Ogale, Satishchandra</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ChemSusChem</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">506-526</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CHEMIZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1864-5631</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are attracting much interest due to their potential as viable future alternatives for lithium-ion batteries, in view of the much higher earth abundance of sodium over that of lithium.  Although both battery systems have basically similar chemistries, the key celebrated neg. electrode in lithium battery, namely, graphite, is unavailable for the sodium-ion battery due to the larger size of the sodium ion.  This need is satisfied by "hard carbon", which can internalize the larger sodium ion and has desirable electrochem. properties.  Unlike graphite, with its specific layered structure, however, hard carbon occurs in diverse microstructural states.  Herein, the relationships between precursor choices, synthetic protocols, microstructural states, and performance features of hard carbon forms in the context of sodium-ion battery applications are elucidated.  Derived from the pertinent literature employing classical and modern structural characterization techniques, various issues related to microstructure, morphol., defects, and heteroatom doping are discussed.  Finally, an outlook is presented to suggest emerging research directions.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp122kud8UHM7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgdF_8CpJO00g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhsl2gtb4%253D&amp;md5=1993d855710123c7f3e134a396dbe052</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref9'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit9" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201700622"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lao, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, S.                         cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Adverse effects of interlayer-gliding in layered transition-metal oxides on electrochemical sodium-ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Yang; Guo, Shaohua; Zhou, Haoshen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">825-840</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Layered sodium transition-metal oxides are the most widely investigated electrodes for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), which are a promising technol. for large-scale static energy storage.  Compared with their lithium counterparts, layered sodium transition-metal oxides exhibit multiple oxygen sublattices depending on the sodium concn., and therefore phase transitions involving rearrangements of the intercalation host frequently occur during charge-discharge.  Herein we summarize existing literature reports on layered sodium oxide electrodes and analyze the effects of host rearrangements on electrochem. properties.  It was demonstrated that phase transitions assocd. with the gliding of transition-metal slabs are unfavorable for battery performance in several crucial aspects, including energy efficiency, rate capability, and cycle stability.  Desirable layered electrodes for SIBs should maintain a stable intercalation host enabling rapid sodium-ion transport within a wide range of sodium concn.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp7JlIMIZoydbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljvbEsbDs9DXg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhtlGhsrfI&amp;md5=e498d76572dadf3dbe20be8456b26518</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref11'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit11" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.6b04577"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hanlon, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Harvey, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Coleman, J.                         cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Liquid Phase Exfoliated MoS2 Nanosheets Percolated with Carbon Nanotubes for High Volumetric/Areal Capacity Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yuping; He, Xiaoyun; Hanlon, Damien; Harvey, Andrew; Coleman, Jonathan N.; Li, Yanguang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8821-8828</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The search for high-capacity, low-cost electrode materials for sodium-ion batteries is a significant challenge in energy research.  Among the many potential candidates, layered compds. such as MoS2 have attracted increasing attention.  However, such materials have not yet fulfilled their true potential.  Here, we show that networks of liq. phase exfoliated MoS2 nanosheets, reinforced with 20 wt % single-wall carbon nanotubes (SWNTs), can be formed into sodium-ion battery electrodes with large gravimetric, volumetric, and areal capacity.  The MoS2/SWNT composite films are highly porous, elec. conductive, and mech. robust due to its percolating carbon nanotube network.  When directly employed as the working electrode, they exhibit a specific capacity of &gt;400 mAh/g and volumetric capacity of ∼650 mAh/cm3.  Their mech. stability allows them to be processed into free-standing films with tunable thickness up to ∼100 μm, corresponding to an areal loading of 15 mg/cm2.  Their high elec. cond. allows the high volumetric capacity to be retained, even at high thickness, resulting in state-of-the-art areal capacities of &gt;4.0 mAh/cm2.  Such values are competitive with their lithium-ion counterparts.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGptS6q-a8cmzrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljvbEsbDs9DXg"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Powder exfoliated MoS2 nanosheets with highly monolayer-rich structures as high-performance lithium-/sodium-ion-battery electrodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Yihui; Chang, Kun; Shangguan, Enbo; Guo, Donglei; Zhou, Wei; Hou, Yan; Tang, Hongwei; Li, Bao; Chang, Zhaorong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Due to their low yield and easy aggregation during the electrode prepn. process, exfoliated MoS2 monolayers cannot fulfill the requirements of alkali-metal-ion battery tests.  Hence, we have developed a facile process to fabricate powder exfoliated MoS2 nanosheets capable of large-scale prodn. and having highly monolayer-rich structures.  This process contains two steps: liq.-phase exfoliation of the edge-rich MoS2 precursor and a freeze-drying procedure.  The proposed MoS2 precursors contain rich edge fractions that are easily exfoliated by this method, and the freeze-drying procedure can maintain the unique monolayer-rich structure of MoS2 in the powder phase.  The electrochem. evaluations of both lithium- and sodium-ion batteries reveal that the proposed powder exfoliated monolayer-rich MoS2 electrode exhibits remarkable specific capacities and stable cyclic performances.  In particular, the monolayer-rich MoS2 nanosheet electrode delivers a superior lithium-storage capacity of ∼1400 mA h g-1.  The exfoliated MoS2 nanosheet electrode can withstand over 1000 cycles even at 1 A g-1.  The mechanism reveals that these unique MoS2 nanosheets not only have a large surface area but also their inclusive monolayer structures exhibit much higher charge mobility than those of bulk MoS2.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq4o9yXL9ExM7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljvbEsbDs9DXg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXis1Snt7jN&amp;md5=73a255ef8ac3fb58253fcc50a8ed693c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201401205"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Su, D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ultrathin MoS<sub>2</sub> Nanosheets as Anode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries with Superior Performance</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Carbon-Reinforced Nb2CTx MXene/MoS2 Nanosheets as a Superior Rate and High-Capacity Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yuan, Zeyu; Wang, Lili; Li, DongDong; Cao, Junming; Han, Wei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">15</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries operating at room temp. have emerged as a generation of energy storage devices to replace lithium-ion batteries; however, they are limited by a lack of anode materials with both an adequate lifespan and excellent rate capability.  To address this issue, we developed Nb2CTx MXene-framework MoS2 nanosheets coated with carbon (Nb2CTx@MoS2@C) and constructed a robust three-dimensional cross-linked structure.  In such a design, highly conductive Nb2CTx MXene nanosheets prevent the restacking of MoS2 sheets and provide efficient channels for charge transfer and diffusion.  Addnl., the hierarchical carbon coating has a certain level of vol. elasticity and excellent elec. cond. to guarantee the intercalation of sodium ions, facilitating both fast kinetics and long-term stability.  As a result, the Nb2CTx@MoS2@C anode delivers an ultrahigh reversible capacity of 530 mA h g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 after 200 cycles and very long cycling stability with a capacity of 403 mA h g-1 and only 0.01% degrdn. per cycle for 2000 cycles at 1.0 A g-1.  Moreover, this anode has an outstanding capacity retention rate of approx. 88.4% from 0.1 to 1 A g-1 in regard to rate performance.  Most importantly, the Nb2CTx@MoS2@C anode can realize a quick charge and discharge at current densities of 20 or even 40 A g-1 with capacities of 340 and 260 mAh g-1, resp., which will increase the no. of practical applications for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqir5qhUHVRo7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljvbEsbDs9DXg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXmvFaqsLw%253D&amp;md5=a340a2233a68f9639c2d0ffda4bbbf0e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2017.04.031"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jia, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wan, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hierarchical Nanosheet-Based MoS<sub>2</sub>/Graphene Nanobelts with High Electrochemical Energy Storage Performance</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchical nanosheet-based MoS2/graphene nanobelts with high electrochemical energy storage performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jia, Yulong; Wan, Hongqi; Chen, Lei; Zhou, Huidi; Chen, Jianmin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">354</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Novel hierarchical MoS2/graphene (MoS2/G) nanobelts were synthesized through a facile hydrothermal reaction.  Here, the MoO3 nanobelts and graphene nanosheets played the important roles in the prepn. of the nanosheet-built nanobelt architecture.  Ascribed to the ordered porous hierarchical nanobelt structure and introduction of graphene, the hybrid electrode exhibits much higher electrochem. capacity than pure MoS2 particles.  The unique ordered hierarchical architecture could greatly relieve the vol. change and stack during the electrochem. process, resulting in the excellent cycling stability.  Specifically, the hybrid electrode possesses a capacitance of 445.71 F/g at 0.8 A/g with a high capacity retention of 96.75% at 2 A/g after 1000 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo7nsekuOqbIbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh8sUUN2qiukA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXlvFClsbc%253D&amp;md5=6755d2fb2a02563f324e8ea439e814f0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201404078"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ao, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Su, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">MoS<sub>2</sub>/Graphene Composite Anodes with Enhanced Performance for Sodium-Ion Batteries: The Role of the Two-Dimensional Heterointerface</span>. <i>Adv. Funct. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>25</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1393</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1403</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">MoS2/Graphene Composite Anodes with Enhanced Performance for Sodium-Ion Batteries: The Role of the Two-Dimensional Heterointerface</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xie, Xiuqiang; Ao, Zhimin; Su, Dawei; Zhang, Jinqiang; Wang, Guoxiu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">25</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1393-1403</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphene has been widely used as conformal nanobuilding blocks to improve the electrochem. performance of layered metal sulfides (MoS2, WS2, SnS, and SnS2) as anode materials for sodium-ion batteries.  However, it still lacks in-depth understanding of the synergistic effect between these layered sulfides and graphene, which contributes to the enhanced electroactivity for sodium-ion batteries.  Here, MoS2/reduced graphene oxide (RGO) nanocomposites with intimate two-dimensional heterointerfaces are prepd. by a facile one-pot hydrothermal method.  The heterointerfacial area can be effectively tuned by changing the ratio of MoS2 to RGO.  When used as anode materials for sodium-ion batteries, the synergistic effect contributing to the enhanced reversible capacity of MoS2/RGO nanocomposites is closely related with the heterointerfacial area.  The computational results demonstrate that Na prefers to be adsorbed on MoS2 in the MoS2/RGO heterostructure rather than intercalate into the MoS2/RGO heterointerface.  Interestingly, the MoS2/RGO heterointerfaces can significantly increase the electronic cond. of MoS2, store more Na ions, while maintaining the high diffusion mobility of Na atoms on MoS2 surface and high electron transfer efficiency from Na to MoS2.  It is expected that the efforts to establish the correlation between the two-dimensional heterointerface and the electrochem. sodium-ion storage performance offer fundamental understanding for the rational design of layered metal sulfides/graphene composites as high-performance electrode materials for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpB50PmkRDAvrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh8sUUN2qiukA"> &gt;&gt; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, T.</span></span>;                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Facile synthesis of hybrid MoS2/graphene nanosheets as high-performance anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Rong; Wang, Jinkai; Li, Chao; Liu, Ting; Yao, Tianhao; Zhu, Lei; Han, Xiaogang; Wang, Hongkang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Ionics</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">26</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">711-717</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">IONIFA</span>;

        </div><div class="casAbstract">We report the facile synthesis of molybdenum disulfide (MoS2) nanosheets on graphene nanosheets (MoS2@GNSs) via simple thermal decompn. of ammonium tetrathiomolybdate in Ar-H2 atmosphere.  When used as anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), the as-prepd. MoS2@GNSs electrode delivers reversible capacities of 389 and 383 mA h g-1 at current densities of 200 mA g-1 and 500 mA g-1 after 200 cycles, resp., which is much higher than that of the MoS2 electrode (253 mA h g-1 after 171 cycles at 200 mA g-1).         </div><div class="casAbstract">2D MoS2 sheets have been extensively served as the anode materials for lithium and sodium ion batteries (LIBs, SIBs) due to its high theor. capacity.                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enhanced sodium storage capability enabled by super wide-interlayer-spacing MoS2 integrated on carbon fibers</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Changtai; Yu, Chang; Zhang, Mengdi; Sun, Qian; Li, Shaofeng; Norouzi Banis, Mohammad; Han, Xiaotong; Dong, Qiang; Yang, Juan; Wang, Gang; Sun, Xueliang; Qiu, Jieshan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Developing advanced electrode materials for effective pseudocapacitive charge storage is one of effective strategies to enhance the rate capability and cycling stability of sodium ion storage devices.                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Chemical activation of hollow carbon nanospheres induced self-assembly of metallic 1T phase MoS2 ultrathin nanosheets for electrochemical lithium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yanguo; Chen, Jiayuan; Xu, Chang; Yu, Tingli; Li, Zhipeng; Wei, Zhiqiang; Qian, Lizhi; Wan, Yanfen; Yang, Peng; Wang, Zhiyuan; Luo, Shaohua; Sun, Hongyu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

High content metallic phase Mo disulfide (1T/2H-MoS2) ultrathin nanosheets with higher intrinsic cond. and extended interlayer distance are vertically assembled on the outer surface of chem. activated hollow C nanospheres (CAHCSs) through a facile solvothermal method. In specific, the CAHCSs@1T/2H-MoS2 electrode delivers a large reversible capacity of 831 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1 after 200 cycles.  At a higher c.d. of 2 A g-1, the CAHCSs@1T/2H-MoS2 electrode has a reversible capacity of 863 mAh g-1.                         cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enhanced lithium storage for MoS2-based composites via a vacancy-assisted method</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Song, Jiawang; Li, Yao; Liu, Zhen; Zhu, Chengling; Imtiaz, Muhammad; Ling, Xin; Zhang, Di; Mao, Jianfeng; Guo, Zaiping; Chu, Shufen; Liu, Pan; Zhu, Shenmin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Applied Surface Science</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Defect engineering, which is a concept applied to exploit the potential of a given material fully, is also considered when designing materials for energy-related applications.  In general, defect engineering focuses on the direct chem. or phys. changes caused by defects through varied mechanisms.  In this study, sulfur vacancies on the surface of molybdenum disulfide (MoS2) nanoflakes are created easily via hydrogen-etching and are employed to improve the composite uniformity and binding condition with tin dioxide (SnO2), which is strongly related to electrochem. performance.  When the as-prepd. MoS2-SnO2 is used as the anode material in a lithium-ion battery (LIB), it delivers a peak capacity of 800 mAh g-1, while retaining a capacity of 580 mAh g-1 in the 1000th cycle at a c.d. of 1 A g-1.  The vacancy-assisted compositing method we propose is demonstrated to be an effective and controllable synthetic technol. and is expected to work in an analogous way for prepg. MoS2 composites with other promising oxide anode candidates (e.g., Fe3O4, CoO, or MnO) in LIB applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqoOLxQhHD8Z7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liuw2yMTFxvvQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXlsFyjsb4%253D&amp;md5=07d947f7eeb52c29f494f6607ed3936a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref26'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit26" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.9b00383"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hierarchical MoS<sub>2</sub> Hollow Architectures with Abundant Mo Vacancies for Efficient Sodium Storage</span>. <i>ACS Nano</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>13</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">5533</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">5540</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchical MoS2 Hollow Architectures with Abundant Mo Vacancies for Efficient Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Yang; Zhang, Rupeng; Zhou, Wei; Wu, Xin; Zhang, Huabin; Zhang, Jian</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Achieving a mol. level understanding of surface performance of nanomaterials by modulating the electronic structure is important but challenging.  Here, the authors have developed a hollow microcube framework constructed by Mo-defect-rich ultrathin MoS2 nanosheets (HMF-MoS2) through a zeolite-like-framework-engaged strategy.  The hollow structured HMF-MoS2 delivers an impressive specific capacity (384.3 mA-h/g after 100 cycles at 100 mA/g) and cycle stability (267 mA-h/g after 125 cycles at 1 A/g) for sodium storage.  As evidenced by expts. and d. functional theory calcns., abundant Mo vacancies in MoS2 can greatly accelerate the charge transfer and enhance the interaction between MoS2 and sodium, resulting in the promotion of sodium storage.  Kinetic anal. result reveals that the ultrafast sodium ion storage of HMF-MoS2 could be assocd. with the significant contribution of capacitive energy storage.  This work highlights the detailed mol. level understanding of chem. reaction on MoS2 surface by defect and morphol. engineering, which can be applied to other metal sulfides for energy storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqUChpnlM2tQLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liuw2yMTFxvvQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXnslGjsbs%253D&amp;md5=1104a770cf6f86e0c3bbd9ead8f3a2a2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1007/s12274-020-3044-x"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Parkin, I.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Supersaturated bridge-sulfur and vanadium co-doped MoS2 nanosheet arrays with enhanced sodium storage capability</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dong, Yuru; Zhu, Zhengju; Hu, Yanjie; He, Guanjie; Sun, Yue; Cheng, Qilin; Parkin, Ivan P.; Jiang, Hao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Research</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The low specific capacity and sluggish electrochem. reaction kinetics greatly block the development of sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  New high-performance electrode materials will enhance development and are urgently required for SIBs.  Herein, we report the prepn. of supersatd. bridge-sulfur and vanadium co-doped MoS2 nanosheet arrays on carbon cloth (denoted as V-MoS2+x/CC).  The bridge-sulfur in MoS2 has been created as a new active site for greater Na+ storage.  The vanadium doping increases the d. of carriers and facilitates accelerated electron transfer.  The synergistic dual-doping effects endow the V-MoS2+x/CC anodes with high sodium storage performance.  The optimized V-MoS2.49/CC gives superhigh capacities of 370 and 214 mAhU+00B7g-1 at 0.1 and 10 AU+00B7g-1 within 0.4-3.0 V, resp.  After cycling 3,000 times at 2 AU+00B7g-1, almost 83% of the reversible capacity is maintained.  The findings indicate that the electrochem. performances of metal sulfides can be further improved by edge-engineering and lattice-doping co-modification concept.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoJ2MkfRab7brVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liuw2yMTFxvvQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXitVWqs7jN&amp;md5=0bc49e993837bfd8a0463b59a9d72365</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2020.124144"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lim, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, S.-O.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Choi, W.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Self-Assembled N-Doped MoS<sub>2</sub>/Carbon Spheres by Naturally Occurring Acid-Catalyzed Reaction for Improved Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Chem.                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Self-assembled N-doped MoS2/carbon spheres by naturally occurring acid-catalyzed reaction for improved sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lim, Hyojun; Kim, Hyeongwoo; Kim, Sang-Ok; Choi, Wonchang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">387</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Molybdenum disulfide (MoS2) has been considered a promising anode material for sodium ion batteries (SIBs) because of its relatively high theor. capacity and 2D-layered structure.  However, the intrinsically low electronic cond. of MoS2 and its severe vol. change during battery operation lead to poor rate capability and cyclability.  In this study, nitrogen self-doped MoS2/carbon spheres (denoted as N-MoS2/C) were easily synthesized through a facile naturally occurring acid-catalyzed method, which takes advantage of the self-doping effect of thioacetamide as a sulfur as well as nitrogen co-source and the self-polymn. property of furfural as a carbon source.  The enlarged interlayer and defect-contg. N-MoS2/C provides not only sufficient active sites to diffuse electrons and sodium ions but also a buffer structure, which can accommodate vol. change during sodiation/desodiation.  The unique structure of N-MoS2/C demonstrates remarkable electrochem. performances, such as high rate capability (charge capacity of 387.9 mAh g-1 at 10 C-rate), superior cyclability (capacity retention of 78% over 200 cycles at 0.2 C-rate), and high-rate cycling (capacity retention of over 96% even after 100 cycles at 1, 2, and 5 C-rate).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoRutisfryjN7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgilApA9ehi5g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXit1Cjs7c%253D&amp;md5=954a94229a4946f2c70982a015b3ef42</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1016/j.jcis.2020.09.055"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.-N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, F.-T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, K.-J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">1T-Phase MoS<sub>2</sub> with Large Layer Spacing Supported on Carbon Cloth for High-Performance Na<sup>+</sup> Storage</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">1T-Phase MoS2 with large layer spacing supported on carbon cloth for high-performance Na+ storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Li-Na; Wu, Xu; Wang, Fu-Ting; Chen, Xue; Xu, Jing; Huang, Ke-Jing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Colloid and Interface Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">583</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">579-585</span>CODEN:

        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0021-9797</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The design and construction of advanced electrode materials is important to the development of high-performance electrochem. energy storage devices.  In this paper, V-doped 1T MoS2 nanosheets with a large layer spacing are grown on carbon cloth (CC) via a one-step hydrothermal method.  The resulting material features abundant edge sites and active centers, and its large layer spacing facilitates the interlayer shuttle of Na+.  Doping with V buffers the vol. change and maintains the integrity of MoS2.  The layered structure of the composite featuring CC as a conductive substrate effectively prevents the agglomeration of MoS2 during the electrochem. process.  When used as an anode material for a Na+ battery, the material displays a high first-cycle irreversible discharge specific capacity of 1234.9 mA-h g-1.  A specific capacity of 453.2 mA-h g-1 is obtained after 100 cycles at a c.d. of 200 mA g-1.  This work provides an effective and eco-friendly route toward obtaining superior MoS2 electrodes for high-performance Na+ storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGokat2ZGB0IF7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgilApA9ehi5g"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pressure-Assisted Interface Engineering in MoS2/Holey Graphene Hybrids for Improved Performance in Li-ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Stolyarova, Svetlana G.; Koroteev, Victor O.; Shubin, Yury V.; Plyusnin, Pavel E.; Makarova, Anna A.; Okotrub, Alexander V.; Bulusheva, Lyubov G.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy Technology (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">10</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1900659</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ETNEFN</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The interface between MoS2 and carbon components plays an important role in the performance of the hybrid material in Li-ion batteries.  To enhance the interfacial interactions, holey graphene (HG) layers are used as a support for the forming MoS2, and the compression of components is used during the synthesis.  Initial compns., obtained by deposition of MoS3 on the surface of HG stacks, are annealed at 400-600°C and 100 bar.  Using a set of characterization methods, the synthesis products are studied and it is found that the hole boundaries anchor MoS2 via covalent C-Mo coupling, while the applied pressure assists in the development of a thin MoS2 coating.  The no. of layers and their lateral dimensions are dependent on the synthesis temp.  The tests of Li-ion half-cells detected higher values of specific capacity for MoS2/HG hybrids synthesized under compression.  Enhanced interaction between the components prevents the destruction of MoS2 during discharging-charging of electrodes, and the capacity increases due to the accommodation of lithium between the layers of MoS2 and HG.  The structural features of MoS2/HG hybrids stipulate growth of specific capacity with long-term cycling to ≈1200 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 0.5 A g-1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpoSiFTfLClR7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgilApA9ehi5g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhvVylsrnP&amp;md5=4c563a53639676f62d5c99e40f46c26d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1039/C8TA09751H"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lin, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Chemically Activated Hollow Carbon Nanospheres as a High-Performance Anode Material for Potassium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Chemically activated hollow carbon nanospheres as a high-performance anode material for potassium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Gang; Xiong, Xunhui; Xie, Dong; Lin, Zhihua; Zheng, Jie; Zheng, Fenghua; Li, Youpeng; Liu, Yanzhen; Yang, Chenghao; Liu, Meilin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">47</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">24317-24323</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Potassium-ion batteries (KIBs) are considered as a promising competitor to other metal-ion battery systems due to their low-cost and large-scale energy storage.  However, their development is hindered by poor intercalation property of K ions in electrodes due to the heavier wt. and larger size of K ion than those of Li ion.  Therefore, achieving an ultra-long cycle life with high capacity and excellent rate capability remains a significant challenge for KIB electrodes.  Herein, activated hollow carbon nanospheres (AHCSs), with enlarged interlayer spacing, oxygen-contg. functional groups (OCFGs) on the surface and high sp. surface area, are proposed as a new anode electrode for high-performance KIBs.  Ex situ XRD and TEM results demonstrated that the enlarged interlayer spacing allow more reversible K ion intercalation into the carbon layer and readily accommodated large (de)potassiation strain without fracture, while OCFGs on AHCSs enhanced pseudocapacitance type behavior and specific capacity.  Due to the synergistic effect of these structural features, the AHCSs served as anode for KIBs, exhibiting impressive electrochem. properties with high initial charge capacity of 370.2 mA h g-1 at 0.2 A g-1, ultra-long cycling life for 5000 cycles at a high c.d. of 2.0 A g-1, as well as prominent rate capability of 137.0 mA h g-1 at 4.0 A g-1.  This study highlights the significant role of interlayer spacing, surface oxygen functionalization and hierarchical porosity of carbon-based anodes in potassium storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr3SE1feG50dLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgilApA9ehi5g"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Aging mechanism of MoS2 nanosheets confined in N-doped mesoporous carbon spheres for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hou, Mingzhen; Qiu, Yongting; Yan, Guanfusheng; Wang, Jinming; Zhan, Da; Liu, Xiang; Gao, Jingchang; Lai, Linfei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">62</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">N-doped hollow carbon nanospheres (NHCS) with mesoporous carbon shells is selected as nanoreactors and encapsulated with few-layered MoS2 nanosheets to monitor its electrochem. properties and structural conversion in long-term cycling.  Mesoporous walls of NHCS can facilitate electrolyte penetration and provide conductive shells for superior mass diffusion and charge transfer.  When serving as SIB anodes, MoS2@NHCS has a capacity value of 371 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1 with a capacity retention of 94.9% after 100 cycles which is higher than powder form MoS2 and is among the highest values of earlier reported MoS2 electrodes.  The origin of gradual capacity decay of MoS2@NHCS anodes in-between 50 to 150 cycles has been investigated.  Transmission electron microscopy and ex-situ X-ray diffraction have shown significant morphol. change of space-confined MoS2 and the prodn. of MoO3 together with oxygen-deficient MoOx after continuous charge/discharge test.  After long-term cycle test of MoS2@NHCS, the ratios of Mo6+ and Mo5+ increased significantly with the decreasing of Mo4+ ratio, while the sulfur from MoS2 transformed from S2- to SO2-4.  This work highlight the phase transformation and compn. change of MoS2 for MoS2-based anode in long-duration charge/discharge tests.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqoFGjffekpYLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljNPa7v-sXVHw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhtVKqt7bM&amp;md5=2a35cb21b6c8d0452ca8cde4ef8f8022</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms10672"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Geng, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Al-Hilo, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Benamara, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Watanabe, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cui, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, T.-p.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Pure and Stable Metallic Phase Molybdenum Disulfide Nanosheets for Hydrogen Evolution Reaction</span>. <i>Nat.                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pure and stable metallic phase molybdenum disulfide nanosheets for hydrogen evolution reaction</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Geng, Xiumei; Sun, Weiwei; Wu, Wei; Chen, Benjamin; Al-Hilo, Alaa; Benamara, Mourad; Zhu, Hongli; Watanabe, Fumiya; Cui, Jingbiao; Chen, Tar-pin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Metallic-phase MoS2 (M-MoS2) is metastable and does not exist in nature.  Pure and stable M-MoS2 has not been previously prepd. by chem. synthesis, to the best of our knowledge.  Here we report a hydrothermal process for synthesizing stable two-dimensional M-MoS2 nanosheets in water.  The metal-metal Raman stretching mode at 146 cm-1 in the M-MoS2 structure, as predicted by theor. calcns., is exptl. obsd.  The stability of the M-MoS2 is assocd. with the adsorption of a monolayer of water mols. on both sides of the nanosheets, which reduce restacking and prevent aggregation in water.                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Micro-spherical CoCO3 anode for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Huang, Guoyong; Xu, Shengming; Yang, Yue; Sun, Hongyu; Li, Zongbei; Chen, Qian; Lu, Shasha</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Materials Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this paper, microspherical CoCO3 powders have been synthesized by the hydrothermal method.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Three-dimensional MoS2/Carbon sandwiched architecture for boosted lithium storage capability</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Chenghao; Ou, Jian Zhen; He, Fengyi; Ding, Jianfeng; Luo, Wei; Wu, Minghong; Zhang, Haijiao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">65</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">104061</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hybrid MoS2/C nanostructures have shown great promise as an ideal anode for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) owing to the improved cond. and electrochem. performance.  Nevertheless, if only one side of MoS2 particles is covered by conductive carbon layer, other exposed side is still low cond.  Meanwhile, the structure of electrodes is relatively not robust.  Herein, an effective structural engineering strategy has been proposed for achieving a new type of polypyrrole-derived carbon nanotubes@MoS2@carbon (PCN@MoS2@C) sandwiched architecture via a facile one-pot hydrothermal process.  When utilized as anodes for lithium storage, the resulting MoS2/C hybrid exhibits a large specific capacity of 1079 mA h g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 and high coulombic efficiency of above 99.0% over 200 cycles, showing a superior cycling stability and reversibility.  The d. functional theory (DFT) calcns. further demonstrate that ultrathin MoS2 nanosheets with an expanded interlayer distance of 0.98 nm have more accessible space, lower transfer resistance, and faster diffusion kinetics of Li ions.  The great improvement in electrochem. properties is mainly ascribed to the design of peculiar hybrid architecture, and the collaborative effect between active MoS2 nanosheets and two different conductive carbon layers.  This work sheds a new light on the rational design of advanced electrode materials with boosted performance and stable structural stability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGolnlLdv3aC2LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljNPa7v-sXVHw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultrathin Metallic-Phase Molybdenum Disulfide Nanosheets Stabilized on Functionalized Carbon Nanotubes Via Covalent Interface Interaction for Sodium- and Lithium-Ion Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Fan, Huilin; Mao, Pengchang; Lan, Gongxu; Liu, Chang; Chen, Jiayuan; Wang, Zhiyuan; Li, Zhipeng; Zheng, Runguo; Liu, Yanguo; Sun, Hongyu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">9440-9449</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAEMCQ</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Two-dimensional (2D) ultrathin MoS2 nanosheets, owing to their abundant active sites, tunable interlayer space, and favored ion and mass diffusion, show promise as anode materials for energy storage.  However, the low electronic cond. due to the intrinsic semiconductor structure (2H-MoS2), the spontaneous aggregation caused by the large van der Waals force between layers, and the huge vol. alteration during the entire reaction hinder the practical applications of MoS2-based anodes.  Here, by employing a facial solvothermal approach, we uniformly disperse metallic-phase MoS2 (1T-MoS2) nanosheets on the functionalized carbon nanotube (CNT) surface to form a 1D@2D hierarchical architecture.  The obtained CNT@1T-MoS2 composites show strong covalent interface interaction and improved electronic cond.  The distinct phase layout, morphol., and component impart the CNT@1T-MoS2 electrode with outstanding sodium-storage performance.  The CNT@1T-MoS2 electrode retains a capacity of 542.3 mA h g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 after 50 cycles.  Even at a large c.d. of 20 A g-1, the electrode still gives a high capacity of 153.4 mA h g-1.  Moreover, when it is applied in lithium storage, the CNT@1T-MoS2 electrode also possesses good stability with a capacity up to 913.5 mA h g-1 experiencing 50 cycles at 0.1 A g-1 as well as satisfactory fast-charging capability (613.6 mA h g-1 at 5A g-1).  This work shows that controlling the phase structure and interface interaction is effective to boost the application of transition-metal dichalcogenide-based composite electrodes in energy storage and conversion.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrtTgrjP8WSLbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg8R_7FwZbpQQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Covalent Assembly of MoS2 Nanosheets with SnS Nanodots as Linkages for Lithium/Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ru, Jiajia; He, Ting; Chen, Binjie; Feng, Yutong; Zu, Lianhai; Wang, Zhijun; Zhang, Qiaobao; Hao, Tianzi; Meng, Ruijin; Che, Renchao; Zhang, Chi; Yang, Jinhu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">59</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">34</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">14621-14627</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ACIEF5</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Weak van der Waals interactions between interlayers of two-dimensional layered materials result in disabled across-interlayer electron transfer and poor layered structural stability, seriously deteriorating their performance in energy applications.  Herein, we propose a novel covalent assembly strategy for MoS2 nanosheets to realize unique MoS2/SnS hollow superassemblies (HSs) by using SnS nanodots as covalent linkages.  The covalent assembly based on all-inorg. and carbon-free concept enables effective across-interlayer electron transfer, facilitated ion diffusion kinetics, and outstanding mech. stability, which are evidenced by exptl. characterization, DFT calcns., and mech. simulations.  Consequently, the MoS2/SnS HSs exhibit superb rate performance and long cycling stability in lithium-ion batteries, representing the best comprehensive performance in carbon-free MoS2-based anodes to date.  Moreover, the MoS2/SnS HSs also show excellent sodium storage performance in sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGomlBu6zto2wLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg8R_7FwZbpQQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhtlShtrjE&amp;md5=63db1ad44bd29627da30a96091b5be98</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1039/C5CP07007D"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiao, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sodium Modified Molybdenum Sulfide Via Molten Salt Electrolysis as an Anode Material for High Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Phys.                         cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium modified molybdenum sulfide via molten salt electrolysis as an anode material for high performance sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Shuai; Tu, Jiguo; Yuan, Yan; Ma, Rui; Jiao, Shuqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Chemistry Chemical Physics</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">18</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3204-3213</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">PPCPFQ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1463-9076</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The paper reports a facile and cost effective method for fabricating sodium molybdenum sulfide nanoparticles through using MoS2 sheets as the precursor by sodium-modification.  The electrochem. performances of sodium molybdenum sulfide nanoparticles are studied as anode materials for sodium-ion batteries.  The galvanostatic charge-discharge measurements have been performed in a voltage range of 0.01-2.6 V vs.  Na+/Na under different current densities, using the as-prepd. sodium molybdenum sulfide nanoparticles as a working electrode.  Typically, the initial discharge and charge capacities of sodium molybdenum sulfide nanoparticles are 475 and 380 mA h g-1, resp., at a c.d. of 20 mA g-1.  The sodium molybdenum sulfide nanoparticles exhibit high capacity with a reversible discharge capacity of about 190 mA h g-1 after 100 cycles.  It should be emphasized that the discharge reaction consists of two steps which correspond to voltage plateaus of 0.93 V and 0.85 V vs.  Na+/Na in the first discharge curve of the Na/MoS2 battery, resp.  But there is only one apparent voltage plateau in the Na/Na-Mo-S battery, and it reduces to below 0.5 V vs.  Na+/Na, which can enhance the power d.  All of the findings demonstrate that sodium molybdenum sulfide nanoparticles have steady cycling performance and environmental and cost friendliness as next generation secondary batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqynUrS1jtUVbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg8R_7FwZbpQQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Dopamine-derived N-doped carbon-encapsulated molybdenum disulfide microspheres as high-performance anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Qiu, Hua; Zheng, Hongyu; Jin, Yuhong; Jia, Miao; Yuan, Qiong; Zhao, Chenchen; Jia, Mengqiu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Ionics</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">26</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5543-5551</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">IONIFA</span>;
